#  [](/thread/71040-quest-100-system)Quest 100 System 

  * 

  * [#1](/thread/71040-quest-100-system "Post Permalink")

  * First Post: Edited Apr 28, 2008 1:25am  Feb 20, 2008 8:57am | Edited Apr 28, 2008 1:25am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

This thread will be an ongoing effort to achieve 100 pips per day (500/week) through the development of an automated EA. Different techniques, indicators and methods will be used from EA to EA. Some indicators may be added, others dropped - all to help us get closer to our goal.  
  
**Goal:** 100 pips per day (500/week)  
**Base Funds:** $5000  
**Restrictions:** Not to blow a $5000 for any given month for the past 12 months. $5000 account balance not to go below $4000 in any given testing month. Work on multiple pairs reliably.   
  
This first post will be used to give important information such as direct links to the current version of EA and other important "quick reference" information.  
  
_**TRADING STRATEGIES**_  
  
**_DANGER ZONE:_** inside the 2 red dotted lines (+20/-20 level of 89SMA) next to the blue line (89SMA) - a lot of whipsaw goes on here as the market consolidates and tries to figure out which direction to go.  
  
**RECOMMENDATION:** DO NOT ENTER a trade from inside the danger zone.  
  
**_MIDDLE OF THE RIVER:_** In between the red dotted lines (+20/-20 level of 89SMA) and the outer bank of the river (+89/-89 level of 89SMA).  
  
**RECOMMENDATION:** Although anything CAN happen, normally the trend is beginning to establish itself. Once you detect the trend is stable, you could enter the trade and exit near/outside the bank of the river it is headed to wards.  
  
**_OUTSIDE THE RIVER BANKS:_** Outside the 2 brown lines (+89/-89 level of 89SMA).  
  
**RECOMMENDATION:** I wouldn't trade while outside these levels but wait till the river comes back into the banks and crosses **_BOTH_** the +/-89 **_AND_** the 13EMA. Once it's on the other side the trend is fairly stable to continue.  
  
**EXCEPTION:** If through other indicators, tools or trading expertise, you have determined that the trend has changed, you may enter a trade outside the banks and gain some additional pips.  
  
**_13SMA "Aura"_**  
Here's how to trade within the 13SMA Aura [http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=209](http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost.php?p=1872512&postcount=209)  
  
**_Known INCOMPATIBLE Pair(s)_**  
The following pair(s) are not compatible with this strategy or the EA.  
  
EUR/GBP  
  
**_Templates/Indicators_**  
  
quest100v_1.3.tpl (Winding River)  
quest100v_1.2gj.tpl (Winding River for GBP/JPY)  
quest100v_1.2gold.tpl (Winding River for Gold)  
i-Sessions pst.mq4 (visual Asia, London, USA sessions on chart)  
  
**_Useful Information_**  
  
Finding your Broker's offset from GMT: [http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...7&postcount=46](http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost.php?p=1863457&postcount=46)  
<http://26z.net/v/132>

  * [#2](/thread/post/1859767#post1859767 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited Feb 21, 2008 5:56am  Feb 20, 2008 9:05am | Edited Feb 21, 2008 5:56am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

Our first version of Quest100_v1.0 will be based on techniques using Fibonacci levels and SMA's.  
  
I call it the **Winding River** method.  
  
**INDICATOR Setup:**  
  
15m chart (start off with USDJPY) NOTE: GBPJPY needs other settings that haven't been tested yet. The 4 majors work fine.  
  
SMA 89 - Median Price - (blue) Levels +89 and -89 (heavier line - brown)  
SMA 89 - Median Price - (color NONE) Levels +34 and -34 (I use dash for levels)  
SMA 13 - Close (red)  
  
Optional: i-session.mq4 (which displays the Asian, London and USA sessions)  
Template: attached template (will need i-session.mq4)  
  
**SIGNAL Setup:**  
  
The SMA89 is our signal line. If the market goes ABOVE we BUY and BELOW we SELL.  
  
**STOP/TAKE PROFIT Setup:**  
  
The SMA13 is used as a guide for the StopLoss. Usually when the market is moving the candle does not fall further than 15 from the SMA13. Thus if we are in a BUY it would be the SMA13 plus 15, SELL SMA13 minus 15 (as a rule of thumb).  
  
TakeProfit - Overflow of a bank would mean the SMA89 would be our goal. Crossing the SMA89 would mean the +89/-89 (outer banks) would be our goal.  
  
Now as common sense would tell us, the SMA's are moving all the time. That's where an EA comes in to monitor them and adjust them till one is penetrated.  
  
  
I've always known the power of Fibs and just out of curiosity I set a few Fib levels on a couple of SMA's and sure enough Fib's RULE!  
  
The next few posts will describe in detail the strategies involved and how the market uses the SMA Fibs as support & resistance.

  * Edited 10:40am  Feb 20, 2008 9:45am | Edited 10:40am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

**_General Overview:_**  
  
As you can see in this chart, the market moves from side to side. The SMA89 and it's 2 levels (+89 & -89 brown) keep it inside the river banks. Several times a month the banks will overflow and the market gets outside these boundary's. This is a PERFECT time to enter a trade in the REVERSE direction for some low risk pips. The market always gravitates trodes the middle of the river (SMA89).  
  
The dashed lines are the +39 and -39 SMA act as support & resistance to a certain extent.  
  
Now we know 3 things so far which can help in designing an EA to watch for certain conditions, reverse if necessary.  
  
1) The market rarely goes outside the +89 & -89 boundary's  
2) The market will gravitate toward the SMA89 center  
3) Often the SMA 39 levels will indicate a consolidation or reversal condition as well as act as soft support & resistance

**_CLOSER LOOK:_**  
  
The cart below is a typical example of how the SMA13 is a good guide for support & resistance and ideal for use as a basis for our StopLoss. In this chart as you can see, the candles never touched it. This is quite common when we just a little momentum to help drive the market. (don't forget we need to add a 15 pip padding to the SMA13 - sometimes a candle may penetrate the SMA13, but not close below it).  
  
**_Quest100_v1.0 EA_**  
  
I have already started developing an EA and with some good results just with the basic rules. I'll be adding some more logic which helps capture even more pips via other "get out if this happens" exit strategies.  
  
Hopefully it should be ready for release in about 2 more days.  
  
Neal  
  
**ATTACHMENT:** This is the optional indicator that displays the Asian, London and USA sessions as background colors.  
  
p.s. By the way - this setup of indicators has great value even if you aren't trading the system or using the EA. It may help you determine whether to get in/out of a trade or when is a good time to reverse.

Neal, just a couple of points. First, in your instructions, at one point you say:  
  
"Now as common sense would tell us, the EMA's are moving all the time. That's where an EA comes in to monitor them and adjust them till one is penetrated."  
  
... But nowhere do you indicate you are using EMA's, only SMA's. This is probably just a typo, so hopefully you can fix it ... Or you can point out how blind I am, since I don't see it.  
  
More importantly, in a case where the price overflows the channel/river, your objective is the 89SMA, right? But what is the SL? Maybe you haven't decided yet?  
  
And, one last question. You say buy or sell on the cross of the 89SMA. I presume you mean on the close of the candle crossing the 89SMA -- but you don't specify, so I thought I would ask. Maybe there could/should be a threshold beyond, so that a longer candle can get us in before the close? That's going to kill us in backtesting, but I'm already seeing, you know, 50 pip 15 minute candle breaks the 89SMA, and your system wouldn't have us jump in until it closes 40 pips beyond the trigger line... then it only continues 8 pips, only to reverse and stop us out with a loss. Same old story... I'm getting teary eyed just thinking about it ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f61c.png?v=15.1):.  
  
Thanks for your efforts.

  * [#21](/thread/post/1861284#post1861284 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 21, 2008 12:40am  Feb 21, 2008 12:40am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar27318_4.gif) Freewheelin](freewheelin)

  * | Joined Dec 2006  | Status: a german in greece | [128 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=27318)

Hi Neal,  
attached a chart showing us not to trade on non-farm-days... I found some more exciting ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f601.png?v=15.1) days where this method would have failed several times.  
But here some suggestions:  
  
Why not add some more fib levels to the SMA and use the 13 SMA as an entry signal?  
I propose to go short when 13 SMA crosses a fib level ABOVE the 89 SMA and vice versa.  
Or going short (and vice versa) when price breaks below a level and the 13SMA changes slope for a certain amount of pips in the direction of the trade? This could be used as filter: Slope change 4pips - no trade, slope change 8 pips - trade.  
  
Maybe we are touched too much by fibonacci? Why not other numbers? Gann for instance used square numbers and roots: 4-9-16-25-36 and so on. Maybe we'll get better results. It would be great to develop an EA which let's us play around with levels and there numbers.  
  
When playing around with the mid-SMA, try 55 with 55 as additional levels to the 89.   
  
  
The suggested method is great - maybe one should predetermine the trend on a higher timeframe and take trades only in one direction, avoiding whipsaws.  
  
Sorry for the idea tsunami ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/270c-fe0f.png?v=15.1)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: killer asia - london 1.gif

The EA is looking GREAT! at this point, just need a little more testing and then will release. You'll be amazed what it's doing!

  * [#30](/thread/post/1862162#post1862162 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 21, 2008 1:54pm  Feb 21, 2008 1:54pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

I can't tell you how excited I am to see that the indicators are appearing to be "universal" (work on many varied pairs with just a few modifications). It's nice to see the market follow the same principals throughout the different pairs.  
  
Keep in mind that if you "tweak" a template for a pair that I haven't listed and wish to post it, the only thing I ask is the values be Fib numbers.  
  
When manually trading the indicators, you will find that you want as many pairs as practical to observe - say perhaps 8. This way you can pick the trades with the highest probability for success. This is when the candles OVERFLOW the banks of the river, take a trade in the opposite direction.  
  
What I did today (manually) was take an OVERFLOW trade on the EUR/USD and the GBP/USD and on the second candle ABOVE the 13SMA I set a 25pip trailing stop and forgot about them. These were the most "stressLESS" trades I have ever done. I wasn't worried in the least that they would result in profit.  
  
Sure enough - it wasn't much (guess I should have set it to 35 pips TS) but EUR/USD was +16 and GBP/USD was +18pips. They are still moving in an upward direction!  
  
By the way.... the EA v1.0 (almost ready - found a bug or two while backtesting) would still be in the trade below. It uses a "buffer zone" below the 13SMA of about 25. This means that it has to fall 25 pips BELOW the 13SMA before it will exit the trade. By observing the 13SMA by scrolling BACK on a chart, you will see that sometimes consolidation takes place and may move down under the 13SMA then start going back up again.

  * [#31](/thread/post/1862171#post1862171 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 21, 2008 2:18pm  Feb 21, 2008 2:18pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

Here's an example of how the EA v1.0 reverses when a river BANK is hit.  
  
(forgive the crude image, but was taken from the EA results and didn't want to take the time to pretty it up)  
  
The white lines are the +89 -89 SMA levels (river banks).  
  
You notice at the bottom it sensed the -89SMA breached and went into a BUY. In this case it was stopped out because it continued down (will be compensated for in the next version of the EA). Then it went back into a BUY.  
  
Once it passed the 89 in the middle of the river, it was stopped out due to the consilidation, but when the market started moving again, it went right back in with a BUY then continued to the top and AUTOMATICALLY REVERSED direction again.  
  
Finally exiting the trade after crossing the 89 in the middle when it sensed the market changing direction.  
  
Total PROFIT from all of these trades (including the bad one at the beginning) was +177 pips.  
  
P.S. By the way, if the EA is currently in a trade when one of the banks are overflowed (+89 & -89 SMA) it automaticlly goes into Trailing Stop mode and rides it up past the bank till it reverses (using a tight 15pip TS) then performs the AutoReverse.

  * Feb 21, 2008 11:38pm  Feb 21, 2008 11:38pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

I have made some minor changes to the templates in post #1 to help make things clearer.  
  
1) quest100v_1.1.tpl - Levels +34 and -34 were changed to +20 and -20 and the color is now red. This level (+20 & -20) was determend after doing a 6 month backtest.  
2) quest100v_1.1gj.tpl & quest100v_1.1gold.tpl - levels remain the same, just changed color to red.  
  
The RED lines are the "buffer zone" (i.e. DO NOT ENTER A TRADE ZONE).  
  
Once a candle has CLOSED outside the RED lines it is a 75% chance you are safe to enter a trade in that direction with high probability that it will continue in that direction (hopefully reaching the +89 and -89 level (banks of river) in order to take a nice profit).

Seeing examples is the best way most people learn something new.  
  
Here is a chart of a trade I took this morning.  
  
The SAFEST entries in this entire system is to catch the retracement AFTER the market has went OUTSIDE the banks of the river (+89 & -89 levels - brown lines).  
  
Once a candle closes BELOW the 13SMA then enter the trade in that direction.  
  
I entered a little early.....  
  
When trading manually, I put a 35pip Trailing Stop on it and forget about it. The desired target will be the 89SMA (blue line in middle), but of course it can go further than that.

#  [](/thread/71040-quest-100-system)Quest 100 System 

  * 

  * [#41](/thread/post/1863182#post1863182 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 3:16am  Feb 22, 2008 12:21am | Edited 3:16am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

**IMPORTANT:** Keep in mind this may not behave as demonstrated in backtesting.... We are moving from the backtesting phase to forward testing. Sometimes things act different than planned.  
  
The Expert Adviser v1.0 is now stable enough and meets the minimum requirements outlined in post #1 (mainly doesn't loose more than $1,000 in a given month - only tested the past 7 months though).  
  
**_BACKTESTING RESULTS_**  
  
Just the figures for now......  
  
$1,928 profit - July 2007  
$3,221 profit - August 2007  
$306 profit - September 2007  
$772 LOSS - October 2007  
$3,207 profit - November 2007  
$1,204 profit - December 2007  
  
Period July 2007 - January 2008 totals:  
  
Pair: USD/JPY  
$8,361 Profit  
Results: <http://26z.net/forex/10.htm>  
  
REMEMBER - this is just v1.0 I know there are a lot of missed trades, premature exits, etc.  
  
The main point is you have something to play with that we can feel fairly safe it won't blow an account or make gross errors in judgment.  
  
v1.1 will have many of these problems corrected and have much better performance and profit.  
  
**_EA is located on post #1_**  
  
  
**_SETTINGS_**  
**NOTE: EA - not for use on GOLD or GBP/JPY till v1.2 (settings are different)**  
  
Most things (stop losses, trailing stops, etc. are handled by logic in the EA)  
  
**MagicNumber** = 304323 MUST BE UNIQUE to this EA (i.e. not the same number as any other EA's you might have running)  
== Start Time ==  
**BeginHour** =8 (GMT) (defaults determined through 6 month backtesting)  
**EndHour** =15 (GMT)  
**GMTOffset** =2 (your broker's difference from GMT)  
  
== Main Settings ==  
**Sensitivity** =18 DO NOT ENTER TRADES above & below this number from the 89SMA (buffer zone - false signals)  
**StopLoss** =35 Stop loss from when a signal is triggered before taking out the trade  
**StopDistance** =30 Has several uses, mainly as a trailing stop  
**autoreverse** =true Automatically reverse a trade when it goes outside the +89 & -89 levels (banks of river)  
**CloseOrdersDaily** =false Close all trades at 00:00 each day (not recommended or tested)  
  
== Money Management ==  
**Lots** =1 Lot size for each trade (i.e. 1.0, .01, .1)  
**MoneyManagement** =false Use money management routines  
**Risk** =10 Percent of account balance to risk on a trade  
  
**NOTE: You may do like I did, and put the EA immedieatly on a chart. If it thinks the conditions are right it may go directly into a trade (even though they aren't ideal). While testing be aware of this and perhaps start the EA either inside the red lines (+20 & -20) or outside the brown ones (+89 & -89). **I'll try to get it to where it doesn't enter immediately on v1.2.

EA managed Trailing Stops & Stop Losses.  
  
Just to let you know, the EA only updates TS and SL every 15 minutes (not like a normal mode of every tick). They should change (if needed) at ??:00, ??:15, ??:30 and ??:45  
  
Under normal circumstances this is adequate. I may build in a sensor that if the market starts moving fast (i.e. if last candle was greater than 30 pips) it shifts into 5 minute mode temporarily.  
  
This cuts down on hundereds of modify orders when it is in every tick mode.  
  
Neal

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

**_FINDING YOUR BROKER OFFSET FROM GMT  
_**(for use when setting your GMTOffset paramater in the EA)  
  
Go to: [http://fxtrade.oanda.com/resources/fxmarkethours/](http://fxtrade.oanda.com/resources/fxmarkethours/)  
Set the time zone to GMT,WET  
Observe the current GMT time (right below where you selected from the drop down menu)  
  
Now in your MetaTrader look at the "Market Watch" window (top left window) which has the different rates ticking away. Your brokers time is at the top of that window.  
  
If GMT says 01:00 and your broker says 03:00 then you have a +2 offset  
  
If GMT says 01:00 and your broker says 00:00 then you have a -1 offset  
  
You would add/subtract the offset from the BeginHour setting of 10:00 to give you the correct EA start time.

Setting broker GMT offset can be confusing sometimes. I think yours is 1 - I know mine is 2 and my broker time is currently 21:39.  
  
I assume you tried the post related to "trying" to demystify GMT offset [http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...7&postcount=46](http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost.php?p=1863457&postcount=46)  
  
Template: Yes 1.1 is current - I only keep the current one posted as not to confuse people.  
  
Have only tested EA with 4 majors and USD/CAD. It will not work currently with GBP/JPY or GOLD due to the volitility. I have to make some adjustments in the EA to accomidate them. You can tell if the EA should work with a pair by putting the basic template (quest100_v1.1.tpl) on it. For example if you put that template on GBPJPY or GOLD you'll see exactlly what I mean.

Smiley face would indicate it is on.  
  
1) At the top of your Metatrader there is a button that says "Expert Advisors", it should be GREEN and sunken  
  
2) click on the X of the EA in the upper right corner of your chart and on the first tab "Common", down at the bottom "Live Trading" should be checked.

> [Quoting et_phonehome_2](/thread/post/1864220#post1864220 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Does the current EA version follow your 13SMA rule?  
>    
>  Other than using the EA, do you have any re-entry rules or would you wait for another signal whereby the entry rules are met?
> 
> Ignored

The only re-entry at this time for the EA would be retracement from either brown line (+89 & -89 SMA) back to the 89SMA.  
  
For manual trading, if you get stopped out (say 35pip trailing stop) once the candles have started gravitating back to the 89SMA you could possibly go back in.  
  
DO NOT REENTER if it is close to danger zone (right now set to 18pips above and below the 89SMA). There tends to be a lot of whipsawing arround the 89SMA.

  * [#78](/thread/post/1865265#post1865265 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 22, 2008 11:32pm  Feb 22, 2008 11:32pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

> [Quoting melpheos](/thread/post/1864757#post1864757 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> The EA is in development... You cannot expect it to be perfect from the start ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)  
>    
>  edit : EA lost 90$ but has 200$ in floating gain. Weird thing is that it has a +96 pips gain on GBPCHF but the SL and TP has been removed after some time ? Is it how it is supposed to work ? (note : the TP set originaly would have been hit by now )
> 
> Ignored

Entry into a trade is fairly straight forward.MAINTAINING and EXITING a trade on the other hand gets a little complicated sometimes.A SL should be in place almost all of the time (can't think of an exception at the moment).The TP is removed when a candle overflows the river banks (+89/-89) to allow it to shift into TrailingStop mode (we don't care how far it goes in the positive direction). The SL is moved on a tight 15pip threshold so we can drain all the pips possible out of the trade when it reverses. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

The EA will make only 1 trade per "MagicNumber". If you have the EA on several charts, check to see that the MagicNumber is different on each. That's how the EA knows which trades belong to it.

#  [](/thread/71040-quest-100-system)Quest 100 System 

  * 

  * [#81](/thread/post/1865511#post1865511 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 23, 2008 1:43am  Feb 23, 2008 1:43am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

I am releasing an "interim" EA Quest100_v1.01 which has several bugs and logic fixes. It is on Post #1.  
  
Be sure before removing the old EA you make note of what the MagicNumber you used was so you can use the same number on Quest100_v1.01  
  
Version v1.1 will be sometime next week - not going to rush it like I did v1.0 now that there is at least an EA out there.  
  
I need to think outside of the box and not be trapped by the normal thinking of setting an EA with fixed StopLoss/TakeProfit levels based on backtesting.  
  
Results from the past 3-6 months are no indication as to what went on in the past 60 minutes. It needs to be intelligent enough to "scale" the TP/SL according to the momentum of the current market.  
  
Finding an entry point isn't the difficult part of a sucessful system, finding the propper EXIT is the goose that laid the golden egg.

  * [#84](/thread/post/1865575#post1865575 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 23, 2008 2:16am  Feb 23, 2008 2:16am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

> [Quoting gioviforex](/thread/post/1865541#post1865541 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi nealc thanks for explanations.....so' if i want trade many pairs in the same platform do i have to change magic number for each pair ?  
>  Thanks for your time
> 
> Ignored

  
That's correct. A MagicNumber tells an EA what trades belong to it.  
  
So you could do something like this:  
  
Chart 1 - EUR/JPY - Magic#: 101  
Chart 2 - USD/JPY - Magic#: 102  
Chart 3 - GBP/USD - Magic#: 103  
  
Putting the same (or different) EA's on a chart and giving them a different MagicNumber allows them to trade independently of one another.  
  
Once the EA is in a stable condition, this will be the way you will want to run for LIVE trading. This way it gives you more trading opportunities.  
  
My theory is to get a good EA that reliablly earns 20-30 pips a day and put it on multiple currencies.  
  
That way 20-30 pips/day on 4 pairs = 80-120pips/day (100 pips/day is my goal).  
  
Of course by accident since you are already in a trade, there will be times 1 pair might make 50-100 pips all on it's own if it is open in the right direction when the market decided to make a big move. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

Hmm.... I hate it when I have these off the wall ideas to solve problems.  
  
**_PROBLEM:_** Backtesting to produce average parameters over a period of time (i.e. 6mo or 1yr) to use as current settings for a forward operating EA.  
  
**_POSSIBLE SOLUTION:_** How about a "self-optimizing" EA that daily reviews say the past 3 days data to recalculate the optimum settings to use. This gives fresh settings based on recent activity to hopefully closer anticipate future patterns.  
  
Just food for thought - in my gut I feel I can code it, but we'll see ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)  
  
**_FEED BACK REQUEST:_** Do you think 3 days is enough, or should it be 7 days, 1 month? What are your feelings. Keep in mind if you go too far back you lose the "freshness" of what's happening in today's market.

**_Tweaking EA:_**

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

> [Quoting vincent001](/thread/post/1866382#post1866382 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> How about a winning EA designed especially for the AUD/USD and NZD/USD markets, Neal ? Not an easy task.  
>    
>  Neal. When will you be releasing the final non demo Quest version ?
> 
> Ignored

Thank you Vincent for asking about the AUD/USD & NZD/USD.  
  
While looking at those pairs with the template zoomed way out, I seen a pattern that I hadn't seen with it zoomed in.  
  
It's funny how the mind focuses on looking for a specific thing and completely misses something obvious (just because your not looking for it).  
  
On a regular basis, there is retracement that we could be taking advantage of. When the market goes ABOVE the +18 level of the 89SMA and then starts back down, it many times will go down to the -18 level of the 89SMA. This may be a prime opportunity for buys/sells on retracement.  
  
PLUS it's the "launching pad" for when the market moves to the +89/-89 levels of the 89SMA (brown lines - banks of the river).  
  
P.S. - I accidently put -20/+20 on the image instead of -18/+18

> On a regular basis, there is retracement that we could be taking advantage of. When the market goes ABOVE the +18 level of the 89SMA and then starts back down, it many times will go down to the -18 level of the 89SMA. This may be a prime opportunity for buys/sells on retracement.
> 
> Ignored

Working on it - LOL  
  
We will be going in "baby steps" with DEMO for a few weeks. v1.1 will contain a single profitable strategy.  
  
The first strategy is where the market is REPELLED by the 13SMA and stays it's distance. Once the market turns, exit the trade.  
  
An EA environment is like the River we trade. It has many trades (fish) that move arround in it. When we introduce a new breed (strategy) we first must be sure that the new breed doesn't disturb the old breed's environment and cause it to suffer negative consequences.

Stops start updating once the market is under/over the 13EMA and the trade is in profit.

2008.02.25 10:00 sell gbpusd @ 1.9624 to 1.9633 -9 pips  
2008.02.25 12:15 buy usdchf @ 1.0906 to 1.0861 -45 pips (stopped out)

Net +8 pips (at least it wasn't a loseing day - lol)

With the exception of the one that was just a plain old bad trade (even from manual standpoint), at least the losses are small.

  * Feb 26, 2008 2:29am  Feb 26, 2008 2:29am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

There's a GOOD setup coming (to trade manually).  
  
**_USD/CAD_**  
  
Once the candle CLOSES above both the 13SMA and the -89 level (brown line) it will be back inside the river banks and headed up!  
  
Enter trade and once +30 profit set a 25pip trailing stop and forget about it.  
  
Taking retracement from the outer banks (-89 & +89 levels --- brown lines) are the safest trades in this whole strategy. Also DON'T PANIC on these if you get in and it goes down 20-30 pips.... it will come back.

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Trader | [145 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=19293)

> [Quoting nealc99](/thread/post/1868273#post1868273 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I agree when "testing" an EA. When "using" an EA to make money, the human has so much more knowlege of things an EA may not be programmed for that closing manually is a good idea.  
>    
>  Let's say your coming up on a Daily/Monthly Support/Resestance barirer. The EA doesn't know that and it might be a good idea to keep an eye on things and close out manually depending on where the market goes.
> 
> Ignored

  
absolutely agree, but premature closing could damage your money management - alot of traders have this problem, when they see even small profit they close the trade and bank it, but when there is loss they let it ride and ruin their acc.  
Since there is a stop loss in this system there is no danger in some losses getting too big, but if you close every so often too early it could reduce profits.  
  
Of course if there is some great resistance on the road of open trades and trade is in profit but all other circumstances show that it is more likely to fail then close it by all means.

I have learned TONS of things in the process of developing this method and some of them I'll be sharing with you in the near future. Would you think I was deranged to tell you that EMA's have "Oras" - LOL - will show you what I mean in the near future.  
  
Right now I'm analyzing to see if the "Oras" have any correlation with each other and how they interact when you have more than 1 EMA in operation. This may be an important key to keeping us OUT of bad trades and getting INTO good trades earlier.  
  
Well sometimes it takes a deranged person to "think outside the box" and not operate within the walls of conventional thinking. How do you think we have some of the wonderful indicators we have today.

> [Quoting moneda](/thread/post/1870087#post1870087 "View Quoted Post")

> Disliked
> 
> Hello Neal and all,  
>  Could someone explain to me why this particular trade was triggered? I am using the most recent EA with defaults settings except for the gmt adjustment. If you look below you will see that it was triggered at 10:15....I don't see the logic behind it based on the entry rules per Neal. Please correct me if I am mistaken.  
>  Thanks
> 
> Ignored

The EA is evolving and being refined faster than the template is updated (my bad).  
  
There is a DANGER ZONE arround the 89SMA (+20/-20) where you get a lot of whipsaw so it will not initiate a trade in that zone even if it has a valid signal.  
  
Once it is past the danger zone and BELOW the 13SMA it looks for 2 PREVIOUS LOWER HIGHS (to further establish a down trend) then it enters the trade.  
  
That appears to be what is seen in the chart.

I understand the danger zone but what I don't understand is why did it enter?......it did not crossed the 89sma(signal line) nor did it go outside the river bank....sorry if I am being thick! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f61e.png?v=15.1)  
  
Keep up the good work! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f647-200d-2642-fe0f.png?v=15.1)

Congratulations!  
  
Just keep in mind - the "danger zone" (+20/-20 level off the 89SMA - blue line) has earned it's reputation through backtestig. There is a lot of whipsawing in that zone while the market decides which direction it wants to go next.

  * Edited 3:12am  Feb 27, 2008 2:53am | Edited 3:12am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

Several PRIME trades coming up!  
  
GBP/USD (see chart)  
USD/CAD  
USD/CHF (may signal in the next few hours)  
EUR/USD (may signal in the next few hours)  
  
GBP/USD - the river has OVERFLOWED the banks (+89 Level of 89SMA) and once it comes back inside the banks AND goes below the 13SMA, that is a signal to SELL.  
  
Same principle applies to the USD/CHF, USD/CAD & EUR/USD if it overflows the banks (buy or sell - depending on which way).  
  
Take the trade in the direction BACK to wards the BLUE line (89SMA).

> [Quoting nicvos](/thread/post/1872146#post1872146 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Why would the EA open this trade?
> 
> Ignored

Any time the market has went "outside" the river (-89/+89 levels of 89SMA) it knows there is a reversal pending. It just took the trade. This is a normal trade with this system.  
  
You can review the **_OUTSIDE THE RIVER BANKS_** strategy in post #1 for more details.

I'll probabbly turn MoneyManagement on at about Risk=5 (5%) and let it manage the lot size.  
  
At least it will take the "human" factor out of the equasion of wanting to do 1 full lot so they can make more.  
  
The MoneyManagement feature works really well, especially once you build up your balance some because it places increasing larger lot size as your balance & risk factor can support (and of course scales back down if you suffer losses).

This is to commend you on this project again.

A USDJPY trade was opened on my demo @ 107.75 yesterday and it was managing it. At a time, I saw a profit target and the SL was also moved. By the time I work up this morning (am in d GMT time zone), I noticed that the TP has been removed and the SL moved to a good level (106.71) locking in profit.  
  
This is a great work and I am sure the live version will be a lot better. But talking seriously, I can do with this for a ride.

  * [#208](/thread/post/1872363#post1872363 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 27, 2008 8:09pm  Feb 27, 2008 8:09pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

Oh, and by the way.... the EA doesn't RULE YOUR WORLD, they are your assistant to help you manage your account when your not around.  
  
For example: My goal is 100 pips/day. Right now the EA has 4 trades going (4 majors) and am up about 80 pips. There's nothing wrong with once I get to 100 pips, I **TURN OFF THE EXPERTS** (so it won't reopen trades) then close my 4 trades manually and achieve my daily goal.  
  
Now knowing me, about a 1/2 an hour before USA session, I'd probably turn the experts back on and let it trade the USA session. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)  
  
NEVER be afraid to take profit, just make sure you TURN THE EXPERT OFF so you don't risk it instantly reopening a position, and due to the timing it turning into a loss.

  * [#209](/thread/post/1872512#post1872512 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 9:56pm  Feb 27, 2008 9:28pm | Edited 9:56pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

Now. Time for some fun......  
  
**CAUTION: Insane person at work!**  
  
Call me crazy and tip over my rocking chair, but did you know that EMA/SMA's have "Oras".  
  
For those whom might not know, an ora is like an invisible energy barrier that surrounds your body. Some psychic's sense it, others have claimed to photograph it.  
  
Anyway, during the EA development process, I stumbled onto something I found quite interesting. I was looking for ways of keeping us out of bad trades and one of the things I was trying was putting levels around the 13SMA.  
  
Quite by accident I noticed a pattern. By putting a +/- level around the 13SMA (in this case I used 13 for a level - fib number you know - LOL) and scrolling through a month, I noticed that the "ora" acted as resistance for BUYS and support for SELLs.  
  
If they fell through their ora, most of the time the trend was broken or weakening and the market started moving the other way.  
  
**NOW WHY DO I TELL YOU THIS CRAZY TALE?**  
  
Well a trader is only as good as the sum of their knowledge, experience and TOOLS. This tool can assist you in when to be cautious and look to get OUT of a trade before it goes bad.  
  
In the image below the PURPLE DASHED line is the +13/-13 level around the 13SMA. If you look carefully you will notice in the middle you will see the candles dip down and ALMOST touch the -13 level (acting as support).  
  
If you look at the end of the chart, you see the candles climbing up getting ready to break -13. Since we are in a SELL this is an "early warning" that the trend may be weakening or coming close to the end of it's life. Once the candle crosses the 13SMA and penetrates the +13 level we can use this as a SIGNAL to exit the trade.  
  
Just for fun, put +13/-13 levels around your 13SMA and scroll back through the days. You will see that sometimes it doesn't hold but a lot of times it DOES. Perhaps a +/-21 level might be better - probably depends on the pair.  
  
Well have fun, and as a reminder:  
  
SELL: -13 level = EARLY WARNING ..... +13 level = GET OUT!  
BUY: +13 level = EARLY WARNING ..... -13 level = GET OUT!  
  
And for those who do not know how to set levels, just click on the property box of the 13SMA and put them in on the LEVELS tab. (not example has 89's for levels - you would put 13 or 21)

MM has to do with the lot size it places.  
  
Most people have a mini account or want to use a very small lot size.  
  
Set LOTS=0.1 (instead if 1). What it will do is adjust your lot size it uses for placing the trade according to your account balance & Risk= setting.  
  
Let's say you have $10,000 in your account and Risk=10 (10%).  
  
When it starts trading it will be placing 1 lot orders. As your balance grows it will place 1.1, 1.2, 1.6, 2, 3,5.5, .... etc. So the EA place more lots on the same trade because your balance is larger and can support the risk if the trade fails. Also if a trade wins, your winnings is multiplied by that lot size factor.

Yes I agree on the backtesting. I have found that results with backtesting this EA are only about 70% reliable (even with 90% data quality).  
  
I think the best thing I've found so far is 3 months at a time. I'm suspecting that if we set our settings with the results of the past 3 months optimized, that may be our best chance for the current month. Will experiment around with that maybe sometime next week.  
  
I still think the best way will be to build in optimization where it determines the best settings say over the past 7 days results. This way the future week can perhaps more accurately be forecast based on the previous 7 days.

  * [#240](/thread/post/1875631#post1875631 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 4:43am  Feb 29, 2008 4:32am | Edited 4:43am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

**IMPORTANT:** Keep in mind this may not behave as demonstrated in backtesting.... We are moving from the backtesting phase to forward testing. Sometimes things act different than planned.  
  
**_BACKTESTING_**  
This EA for some reason does not backtest well. I have see it do odd things (like not take trades that met the exact conditions necessary  
  
**_SETTINGS_**  
**NOTE: EA - not for use on GOLD or GBP/JPY till v1.2 (internal settings are different)**  
  
**MagicNumber** = 304323 MUST BE UNIQUE to this EA (i.e. not the same number as any other EA's you might have running)  
  
  
**== Start Time ==**  
**BeginHour** =8 (GMT) (defaults determined through 6 month backtesting)  
**EndHour** =20 (GMT)  
**GMTOffset** =2 (your broker's difference from GMT)  
  
**== Main Settings ==**  
**Sensitivity** =18 DO NOT ENTER TRADES above & below this number from the 89SMA (buffer zone - false signals)  
**Sensitivity12H** =11 Distance ABOVE 13SMA to open BUY or close a SELL  
**Sensitivity12L** =8 Distance BELOW 13SMA to open a SELL or close a BUY  
**TakeProfit** =35 Take Profit (trailing) Moves UP by setting for a BUY but not down (opposite for a SELL)  
**StopLoss** =35 Stop loss (trailing) Moves UP by setting for a BUY but not down (opposite for a SELL)  
**StopDistance** =30 Does not place a BUY/SELL if it is this distance INSIDE the banks of the river (+89/-89 levels of 89SMA)  
**CloseOrdersDaily** =false Close all trades at 00:00 each day (not recommended or tested)  
  
**== Money Management ==**  
**Lots** =1 Lot size for each trade (i.e. 1.0, .01, .1)  
**MoneyManagement** =false Use money management routines  
**Risk** =10 Percent of account balance to risk on a trade  
  
**EA is located on post #1**  
  
**NOTE:** Sometime the EA will get into a trade "before" the trend starts to change. I know several times it may have went -10 -25 pips then recovered to end up in a profit. Yes, there are times it will end up stopping out, but just because it goes down, more times than not it will recover.  
DO NOT BE AFRAID to take out a trade when it looks like the trend is about to change. My goal is 100 pips/day and if I get to that level, turn the EA *OFF*, exit the trades, then start it back up after midnight GMT to harvest another day's pips. The EA is a "tool" to help you get into trades when your not monitoring the market and to take trades out if you're not around. By all means if you've reached your goal for the day or see indication the trend is changing - BY ALL MEANS CLOSE OUT THE TRADES!

Yes, think of th MagicNumber as a street address. Each EA's street address must be different so it know what trades belong to it.  
  
If you have everyone living at the same address the EA will have bad results (like trailing stops on for EUR/USD based on GBP/USD figures and they will be fighting each other).

It's the chemistry of the "mechanical" EA and the ability of the human trader that will make you money in the long run.

> [Quoting kdrugan](/thread/post/1876683#post1876683 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I'm a bit confused by the MM system in the EA here - should you be using the Lots and Risk settings together? Or does the EA auto calculate what Lot size to be using if you have MoneyManagement=true and Risk set?  
>    
>  Thanks!  
>    
>  \- Kevin
> 
> Ignored

Yes, that's a little confusing isn't it. I will move Lots= up under a different category.  
  
Lots= is used regardless if you have MoneyManagement enabled or not so you can control how many lots it uses for each trade.  
  
If MoneyManagement is TRUE, it doesn't even look at the Lots= setting. It will do it's calculation and the minimum will be 0.1 if your account balance is too low. (Maximum will be 99).

> 
> Disliked
> 
> Excellent!  
>    
>  And the Risk % is on a per trade basis, or in terms of how many trades the EA will allow you to have open full stop? I'm reading it as per trade, but wondering if there's some way to limit how many trades in total the EA could have you in.
> 
> Ignored

Risk= and the balance of your account determine the lot size calculation - so it doesn't matter if you have 10 EA's running it always looks at your account balance * Risk= (which is a percentage) to determine lot size.  
  
Each EA (Quest EA at least) should only allow 1 trade open per MagicNumber.

It is probably fine.  
  
Uninit5 states that you changed the parameters (perhaps the magicnumber after it had a smiley face) and it was just restarting the EA:

No, it normally will not start a trade immediately now. I've only had 2 trades so far today since 8:00 GMT and none are currently open.  
  
The "demo" statement always appears when the EA first starts in the journal. You would also get an ALERT box if you tried to put it on a live account.

  * Mar 1, 2008 3:01am  Mar 1, 2008 3:01am 

  * [ mrkam](mrkam)

  * | Joined Aug 2006  | Status: Trader | [169 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=17053)

Is 20p a day per pair reasonable? I would say not really.... Only because it just isn't done. Anywhere. That would be 5,200per year, every year, per pair. Trading 5 pairs, 26,000p per year??? Reasonable?? Well, if so, why isn't it being done by reasonable traders? Even pros don't even get CLOSE to that!!   
  
Amongst us traders that make a living on this, we can live quiet well on 150p a week. (not a DAY!).... And that for for ALL of our trades, not just one pair. Now THIS apprears to be quite reasonable. (5 pairs, net +30p per week per pair...) Our forward testing will give us an indication of what we can expect, and so far, we're not there yet... much less 20p per day per pair, every day.  
  
Look, we don't need 26,000p per year. We don't need to turn $1k into a million $ in a year. If this system can generate 100+p per week, which it has a decent chance of doing, but not without some work and trade management on our part, then you have a GREAT system...   
  
We don't need to sensationalize it with outrageous claims.. it appears to be good enough on it's own.

Much superior version of EA in process (v1.2). Been concentrating on it because I'm just not satisfied with how v1.1 is behaving (or performing).  
  
I found that I looking so close at the "aura" on the 13SMA that I completely missed the aura on the 89SMA. 1) they are not in harmony currently, 2) using the 89SMA aura completely eliminates the need for the 13SMA and gives you much bigger/safer entires/exits.  
  
With the 89SMA the trades are longer than the 13SMA - many are overnight.  
  
So you can see the 89SMA aura I've put up an image. I won't go into explaining much detail at this point, but you can probably figure it out by closely studying it. I have put up Quest100v_1.3proto template up so you can play around with it and use it to glance back in history.  
  
In the image below - Trade 1 yielded 47 pips... Trade 2 yielded 52 pips... Trade 3 (NFP retracement) yielded 53 pips.  
  
There are other trades in this image but those were the safe ones.  
  
NOW by adding the 12SMA aura principle on the first trade we could have went ALL THE WAY TO THE BOTTOM yielding 153 pips.

  * Mar 2, 2008 4:22am  Mar 2, 2008 4:22am 

  * [ vincent001](vincent001)

  * | Joined Feb 2008  | Status: Trader | [80 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=61144)

Sounds good Neal, and yes v1.1 doesn't seem to be up to scratch and is performing rather poorly.  
  
My experience with EA's is that you need to have a good Stop Loss in of around the 35-50 point mark and make the Take profit around the 10 - 20 point mark. Now this may not sound great but believe me if you are winning 95% of your trades then a small loss here and there will not offset the wins that you are having. Now don't get me wrong here, winning 50-80 points is great but it's not always that easy to do this consistently. Better to take a smaller profit and lock it in. If an EA is good enough it can always execute another trade for the same pair(s) anyway.  
  
My experience working for a FX Company (turning over 5 billion per annum) and watching the fundamentals day in and day out is that you must have a Stop Loss on. EA's that rely on the market coming back around again are not guaranteed as the draw downs can be massive.   
  
By the way, and for those of you who are interested, Online Brokers love people who use Expert Advisors as they use their platforms and hence spend money. It's ABOUT money in THEIR bank accounts.   
The reality is is that 95% of people who use EA's probably lose their money. The small percentage of people who do use winning EA's are few and far between. The ones that are using winning EA's are invariably not spending big money anyway so Brokers are not overly concerned.  
  
People like Neal here will eventually develop a good EA but again Brokers are not overly concerned about this as the money they make from the payments that come in is what makes them happy.  
  
  
  
Food for thought.

> hey i really like wat u are doing here, just wondering if you ever thought of the crossing of the 13 and the 89 would be a good exit signal. just a thought =)
> 
> Ignored

  
13/89 crossing is a good "early warning" to start paying attention to a possible trend change.  
  
There's a lot of "sluggishness" around the 89 while the market decides on it's next direction (in a lot of cases).  
  
I have found that it is safest to trade from the "outer fringes" and gravitate BACK to the 89 in trades. Quite often you get the "sling shot" effect where it will just go right through the 89 like a hot knife in butter. That's the nice trades to be in and stay in.  
  
ADDENDUM: Misread your post (must be tired - LOL) Yes it is a good exit signal.

>  If you need a good broker where you can get in for very little (i.e. $100 to be safe) there is the broker I use on the next to the last page of the presentation. (Press the "H" button on the navigation icon and it will take you to the table of contents, then you can go right to the page).  
>    
>  Attached are my 3 trades:  
>    
>  EURUSD +40  
>  USDCHF +7 (aborted - got scared - lol)  
>  USDCAD +30  
>    
>  Oh did I mention (no, guess I did not) - my LIVE account balance is up over 15% from since Feb 26th (that's 6 CALENDAR days for those of you who read the thread in a month from now).
> 
> Ignored

Oh you ask how do I make all these nice looking screenshots?  
  
There's a WONDERFUL little tool out there called Jing by Techsmith which is absolutley FREE. It lets you snap a segment of your screen (like a graph) than has annotation tools to let you type and draw symbols.  
  
It's on this page <http://allonq.com/links.php> under "Jing Project".  
  
There's also one called Evernote which comes in handy as well.

  * [#320](/thread/post/1884073#post1884073 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 5, 2008 4:42am  Mar 5, 2008 4:42am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

> [Quoting papagenu](/thread/post/1884041#post1884041 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I just found this thread today and have found it a very interesting read. Looking forward to trying out the EA on a demo when I get home tonight. One question, does the EA leave trades open over the weekend or does it close out any open trades when the market closes on Friday?
> 
> Ignored

The EA only closes on a signal. So if you have a trade open on Friday and there's no signal to close, it will remain open and continue to trade Sunday when the market opens back up. (you can close them out manually on Friday if you wish).  
  
All you new people - be sure to watch the Aura Training - URL is in Post #1   
  
It's about 30 minutes long but will be well worth your time in understanding exactly the system works.

I do agree though that I would be cautious getting this late in the market session. There will not be as much activity and the river could turn even though the market don't move much (you know how SMA's gravitate to what the market is doing). Of course since it's AUD/USD and Sydney market is one of the first to open you will probabbly be fine... noticed it's up to 0.9259 and moving up.  
  
I am currently in a USD/CAD SELL that I feel comfortable with (got into a little while ago when price was at 0.9950 (17:24 GMT) when it ALMOST touched the signal, then started going back down.... then went back up and pierced through the SELL signal.

Great Job! on the 45 pips...  
  
The trade would have been entered on the 89SMA BUY signal, but since it was going good when it got up to the exit point we have the option of continuing in the trade by shifting over to the 13SMA rules then exiting based on them.  
  
If you can sustain 2 lots (depends on the size of your account) - yes it's always good to do 2 lots on a GOOD trade and exit 1 and let the other trailing stop out.

> [Quoting seamonkey](/thread/post/1886552#post1886552 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I'm a little confused, can you tell me why the EA would take this as a buy signal for AUDUSD?
> 
> Ignored

EA v1.1 bases it's buys on:  
  
EMA12+Sensitivity12H < EMA89-Sensitivity && High[1] <= EMA12-Sensitivity12L  
SMA13 plus the +21 level is less than SMA89 minus the Sensitivity setting  
  
*** AND ***  
  
the previous candle's HIGH is less than SMA13 - Sensitivity12L setting  
  
Aren't you glad you asked - LOL - I get a headache just looking at it.

  * Mar 6, 2008 4:28am  Mar 6, 2008 4:28am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57770_4.gif) nealc99](nealc99)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

TEXTBOOK example of when to swtch from your 89SMA strategy over to your 13SMA strategy for your EXIT.  
  
We started on an 89SMA BUY signal to get into the trade.  
  
When we were at the 89SMA EXIT signal we "evaluate" how the 12SMA strategy is doing. In this case all conditions were GO to switch over to the 12SMA strategy, so we STAY IN THE TRADE and look for our 12SMA EXIT signal.  
  
As you can see this one was a beauty and would have yielded around 135 pips!  
  
Right before exiting an 89SMA trade, look to see if you would be still in a 12SMA trade. Maximize your profit and still keep your risk minimized.

>    
>  I STILL FIND IT HARD DETERMINING when to get into a trade. If I take a risk and enter a position at the Brown line the markets sometimes still goes down below by over 100 points (extreme case). Then I have to worry about how long it stays down and whether not the gain it makes is worth it at all.  
>    
>  IS there no rule of thumb regarding this ?
> 
> Ignored

It can be tricky sometimes. I have added 2 slides to the avBook addressing the issue of "undercurrents" in the river, the danger of using the BROWN LINE as a early entry signal and an example of how a VALID signal can result in a negative balance exit (happens rarely).  
  
Review this page and then do NEXT ( > ) to see the 2nd entry added. (narrated slides). [http://allonq.com/pr/4128&s=24](http://allonq.com/pr/4128&s=24)  
  
Everybody ready for NonFarm Employment Change? Don't forget - the system (usually) does NOT give a signal for the initial surge, but we trade the "retracement" going in the opposite direction after the market has peaked out. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

Here is one of the trades we took this morning in the LIVE trading session.  
  
ENTERED once the large upward spikes settled down due to NonFarm Employment Change, then continued in a downward trend till it "almost" (within 1-2 pips) touched the exit line. A little later it produced a clean exit by piercing the exit line.  
  
Trade would have yielded +34 pips (I got a little trigger happy and set a tight 15pip stop loss which took us out a little early). Hey, I'm still learning too - LOL  
  
Be sure and **_MONITOR_** USD/JPY and EUR/JPY - they are positioning themselves for SELL signals over the next hour or two.

> [Quoting bimboforex](/thread/post/1898877#post1898877 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> hi neal,  
>  what if the candle pierces thru but does not close below or above for sell or buy, do i still enter the trade or i have to wait till it closes below or above.
> 
> Ignored

"Piercing" would be an "early entry", but as you can see in this example, the "pierce" of the signal didn't take. It ended up going up +50 pips before starting to come back down.  
  
NOTE: The exception to the rule would be if the 13SMA is a long ways away from the red/green dashed line when you get a signal. This is usually due to a large move and we are having retracement. It's ok to get in then without passing both.

Finally starting to see the light at the end of the tunnel on the Aura Indicator.  
  
It offers SELL/BUY signals with regular/email alerts.  
  
Below is an example of what it looks like. In this case it gave a SELL signal and when the red bar turns gray it's time to exit. This trade would have yielded +65 pips. (most trades are from 20-40 pips)  
  
Tomorrow I'll start testing in forward trading. I know of a few bugs to still work out. Will try to have v1.0 out Sunday/Monday so you can start testing.  
  
Thanks!  
Neal  
  
p.s. This is a good reason to trade several pairs. The more pairs the better chance of a few signals per day. Looks like it's averaging 1-2 trades/day per pair. Some days there are no trades for a single pair.

  * Mar 15, 2008 8:43am  Mar 15, 2008 8:43am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar35798_13.gif) Pip](pip)

  * | Joined Mar 2007  | Status: Trader | [45 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=35798)

I am posting a real trade made yesterday on EURJPY .   
On Point 1 you can see the sell setup . The trade starts running and after some time price do a small reversal. Here we can see something special. Point 2 show how SMA13 act as a resistance a little above the 50% Fibonacci retracement level. Price tested two times 50% Fibonacci level retracement and then went down till the estimated target area  Point 3.   
Here I was facing a trading dilemma  close position or stay in the trade the last price bar was a big one and __perhaps__ price can continue down. So .., I decided to stay in the trade.   
Then price start to move up during 3 bars  Point 4, and start to move down as I __desired._ _ Ok, It was another up retracement and now it will go down to make another lower low  I thought But reality is quite different from ours wishes, thoughts and expectations and position was closed at breakeven.  
What is important here to note is that it was a very nice price move that behaved according to Neal system and we were able to see SMA13 importance and how a price target was meet.  
Have a nice weekend!!  
Pip

  * [ mrkam](mrkam)

OK... but (and I love fibs!).... Isn't our conservative entry on the 89 system to enter at the first close below the 89 aura after a break of the 89 River bank? (your red dashed line...)  
  
In which case our entry would be at the OPEN of the candle AFTER yours marked #1.... at about 730... Then, the exit is at the touch of the upper blue aura (on your chart) at about 680... your candle #3.   
  
Very vanilla.... and 50pips!!! no real dilemma... eh? Interesting to see the 13 act as resistance, but not really an issue trading the 89 system... only got to 735...  
  
Nice and simple... the way to trade...!! I'm all for getting the big moves... but only IF they happen within my trading plan. If not, I have a stop loss plan. But here, 50pips, no fuss, no muss.   
  
I know the "goal" is 100p per day. But really, 150p per week is GREAT, and one can live quite well on that. Trying to get too much is the greed part, and will KILL us... really.. been there. To the tune of 70K... but still alive to trade!!  
  
And this is ALL just my opinion... please!

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [292 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57770)

Doing good guys! Your seeing patterns according to the system.  
  
So there was no confusion, I commented on the chart with the correct entry/exit points outlined by the system so it would be clear.  
  
SELL ENTRY is below the red dashed line and below the 13SMA (unless the 13SMA is far away due to rapid movement).  
  
EXIT is the gray dashed line (blue on this chart) just above the 89SMA.  
  
NOTE: the 2nd trade is an ideal example of evaluating a trade before exit. As we can see we could have shifted over to the 13SMA system and stayed in the trade a while longer for extra safe pips.  
  
Thanks again for all your interest and support for the system.  
  
Neal

Great work Neal, but I would like to advise all traders to be careful where they put their money when it comes to "online" Brokers. No matter how good a trading system is, this can all be taken by a crooked Broker. This is very important at this time as the US in particular is in real trouble and financial companies are in real trouble.  
  
For 10 years now we have been predicting a deep recession/depression and it's all coming true. In fact we have timed it for exactly now, and we are now predicting a depression or a series of recessions. Folks, this is a serious problem and it will make the 80's recession look like a joke. Buy gold, silver or important commodities like coffee, tea and sugar. Having travelled the world and knowing many Merchant Bankers, my advice is simple, be very careful where and how much money you trade with at this time.   
  
Don't let Bush, Fed or anybody else fool you. They lie about everything. The US is going down BIG TIME and so is the majority of the other countries out there. UBS (Switzerland annouced they are laying off 8,000 jobs today). Get my drift !  
  
Neal. I apologise for digressing on your great trading system but Traders have to be aware that no matter how good your system is they need to be very careful with their money at this point in time.

Today was one of thoes "in the right place at the right time" Asian sessions.  
  
When "outside" the river banks, anything can happen, but I would have traded off the 13SMA method and would have resulted in about +110 pips.

I have ended up SWAMPED with work this week and haven't had much time to clean up the indicator & EA.  
  
The performance is not good at this point.  
  
I'm going ahead and releasing the source for the indicator so that perhaps some other EA programmer can troubleshoot and round off the rough edges.  
  
70-80% of the time it does fine for a "guide" of when to start monitoring the market for a valid signal. Most of the signals are on the 13SMA.  
  
Things to be added: Alert when signal occurs & email alert.  
  
**CAUTION: Indicator is "beta" and you should use your judgment to override if necessary.**

> 
> Disliked
> 
> How to set the indicator?
> 
> Ignored

The only setting you would want to change is the Eatime which is the TF on which the indicator is applied.  
  
If you set it on M15, Eatime should be 15.  
On hourly, eatime should be 60 and so on.

Today morning I performed 3 trades, 2 losing trades (EURJPY) and one wining trade (USDJPY).   
  
I entered EURJPY at point 1 and after some time I stoped and reversed at point 2. The short trade was running well and I changed my Initial Stop loss to reduce trade risk. Then news came and I was stopped again with a minor loss.   
USDJPY short was my best trade using Quest 100 system. Thank God!!  
  
Have a nice day!  
  
Pip

The indicator does appear to be very unstable and it does "repaint" I would not attempt to use it for trading as a stand alone indicator. Just place it on a short timeframe and you will see what happens - remember to change the indicator parameters.

Just to let you know, I'm still arround and trading the system on a daily basis. It still out performs most systems I've seen.  
  
Made +107 pips yesterday - LIVE account!  
  
Most days are 50-80 pips.  
  
Have decided that there are too many "nuances" for an EA to be able to deal with (market news, slow times of the market day, and several others that I've picked up by manually trading).  
  
I'm removing the EA from the first post at this time.  
  
This system is best traded manually with judgement calls on the part of the trader.  
  
Anyone else using the system?
